Permissibility of Hunting and Its Proofs
Opens the Book of Hunting with definition, permissibility ruling, and three transmitted proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hunting and identify the three transmitted proofs (Quran and hadith) that establish its permissibility and conditions.

Core Idea
Hunting is permissible outside ihram and the Haram, but only with tasmiyah and proper means.

This lesson opens the Book of Hunting in the Hanafi legal tradition. The author defines sayd, the act of hunting, and immediately clarifies its default ruling: it is halal for those not in ihram and not inside the sacred precincts. The lesson then examines the Quranic and Prophetic proofs that ground this ruling, including the key conditions for lawful hunting with trained dogs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage defines sayd and states it is mubah (permissible) for a non-muhrim outside the Haram.
The ruling is explicit: 'الفعل مباح لغير المحرم في غير الحرم'.
2
Locate the first Quranic proof
Verse 5:2 ('When you become halal, then hunt') indicates permissibility after ihram, using an imperative after prohibition.
The imperative implies ibaha (permission) per Hanafi usul.
3
Locate the second Quranic proof
Verse 5:96 ('Forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram') explicitly forbids hunting in ihram, implying permission otherwise.
This establishes the condition: not in ihram.
4
Extract the hadith proof
The hadith of Adi ibn Hatim conditions lawful hunting with trained dogs on tasmiyah, the dog not eating the game, and no other dog joining.
The hadith provides detailed conditions for consumption.
5
Note the explanatory notes
The Urdu commentary emphasizes the two primary conditions (not in ihram, not in Haram) and notes that these are three of five proofs.
The author mentions two more proofs later.

Chapter of Hunting. Translation: This chapter is about hunting. Explanation: Just as drink brings pleasure, similarly hunting brings pleasure and joy (as is not hidden), so the basis of suitability between them is apparent. Also, hunting is among foods, whose suitability with drinks is apparent. Then just as some drinks are halal and some haram, similarly among hunting some are halal and some haram. Then the reason for giving precedence to drinks is that in it the predominance is of prohibition, and in this (hunting) the predominance is of permissibility (as is apparent). The lexical meaning of sayd and three proofs for the permissibility of hunting: Sayd is hunting and is applied to what is hunted, and the act is permissible for one who is not in ihram in other than the Haram, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And when you become halal, then hunt', and due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram', and due to his saying, peace be upon him, to Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i, may Allah be pleased with him: 'When you send your trained dog and mention the name of Allah upon it, then eat; and if it eats from it, then do not eat, because it only captured for itself. And if another dog joins your dog, then do not eat, because you said the tasmiyah upon your dog and did not say it upon the other dog.' Translation: Sayd means to hunt, and it is also said for the animal that is hunted. And this act is permissible for one who is not in ihram in other than the Haram, due to the command of Allah Most High: 'And when you become halal, then hunt', and due to the command of Allah Almighty: 'And forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram', and due to the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, to Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i: When you send your trained dog and you have mentioned the name of Allah upon it, then eat. But if the dog has eaten from it, then do not eat, because the dog has captured for itself. And if another dog joins your dog, then do not eat, because you said the tasmiyah upon your dog and did not say it upon the other dog. Explanation: Sayd has two meanings: 1) hunting, 2) the animal that is hunted. Then hunting is a permissible act, but the condition is that the hunter should not be in a state of ihram and should not hunt in the Haram. The author has mentioned five proofs for the permissibility of hunting; three are in this phrase that is mentioned, and two after this. These three proofs are transmitted (naqli), the first two are verses of the Quran and the third is a hadith. From the first verse it is known that in the state of halal (non-ihram) hunting is halal; from the second it is known that in the state of ihram hunting is haram; and in the hadith further details are mentioned, which are apparent from the translation.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Hunting (Kitab al-Sayd) in Ashraf Ul Hadaya, a Hanafi commentary on Al-Hidayah. The author first explains why the book on hunting follows the book on drinks: both involve pleasure (surur) and are related to food and drink. Then he presents the core ruling: hunting (sayd) is permissible (mubah) for a person not in a state of ihram (muhrim) and outside the sacred precinct (al-Haram). The Arabic matn defines sayd as both the act of hunting and the animal hunted. It then provides three textual proofs for permissibility: two Quranic verses and one hadith. The first verse (Al-Ma'idah 5:2: 'When you become halal, then hunt') indicates permissibility after exiting ihram. The second verse (Al-Ma'idah 5:96: 'Forbidden to you is game of the land as long as you are in ihram') implies prohibition during ihram, thus permissibility otherwise. The hadith from Adi ibn Hatim specifies conditions for hunting with a trained dog: the dog must be sent with tasmiyah (saying Bismillah), and if the dog eats from the game, it is not halal because it captured for itself rather than the hunter. If another dog joins, the game is not halal because the hunter did not intend to use that dog. The Urdu commentary elaborates that these are three of five proofs the author mentions, the other two coming later. The commentary also clarifies that hunting is only permissible if the hunter is not in ihram and not in the Haram. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah of the Hanafi school, based on clear Quranic texts and the hadith.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Hunting or the animal hunted. The text says it is applied to both the act and the prey.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, during which hunting is prohibited.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct around Makkah and Madinah, within which hunting is prohibited even for non-muhrim.
كلب معلم (kalb mu'allam): A trained dog that hunts for its owner and does not eat the game unless allowed.
تسمية (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah) at the time of releasing the dog or shooting the arrow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, for whom is hunting permissible?
A) Anyone at any time
B) A person not in ihram and outside the Haram
C) Only while in ihram
D) Only inside the Haram

Key Takeaway
Hunting is mubah for a non-muhrim outside the Haram, with additional conditions for consumption of game, such as tasmiyah and the animal not eating from it.

The Proofs for the Permissibility of Hunting
Opening the book on hunting with proofs of permissibility and listing conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two proofs (ijma and istihsan) for the permissibility of hunting in the Hanafi school and explain why the baseline ruling is mubah.

Core Idea
Hunting is mubah by consensus and because it is a benefit for the mukallaf, like gathering firewood.

This lesson examines the foundational proofs that the Hanafi school uses to establish the permissibility of hunting. While many assume hunting is allowed, the school provides explicit evidence: the consensus of scholars and a reasoned analogy to other permissible activities. Understanding these proofs helps clarify why hunting is not inherently haram or wajib, but a neutral act that becomes conditioned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its baseline ruling
The act is hunting (sayd). The Hanafi school rules it as mubah (permissible). This is the default position before considering any conditions.
The passage states: 'وعلى اباحته القعد الاجماع' – consensus has been established on its permissibility.
2
Examine the first proof: Ijma'
The text claims that the permissibility of hunting is established by consensus (ijma'). In Hanafi usul, ijma' is a definitive proof (qat'i al-dalala).
Ijma' is valid only when all qualified mujtahids agree. Here, it is presented as an established fact.
3
Examine the second proof: Istihsan
The second proof is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The passage argues that hunting is a type of earning (iktisab) and benefit (intifa') from animals created for that purpose. It also preserves the mukallaf so that he can fulfill religious obligations.
This is analogized to gathering firewood (ihtitab), which is also mubah. The analogy shows that hunting is a lawful means of sustenance.
4
Recognize the restricted nature of the ruling
Even though the baseline is mubah, the passage immediately follows with fifteen conditions that must be met for the hunted animal to be halal. This shows that the permissibility is not absolute but conditional.
These conditions are detailed in the next lesson. Here, note the structure: the ruling is established, then the restrictions are listed.
5
Determine the authority and mufta bihi
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as quoted from al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir. The mufta bihi position is that hunting with trained animals is permissible provided all conditions are met.
The passage ends by affirming hunting with trained fanged beasts and clawed birds is permissible, quoting established texts.

كتاب الصيد
۳) وہ شکار ایسا ہو جو اپنے بازو اور پنجوں سے یاسینگوں وغیرہ سے) اپنی جان کی حفاظت کرنے والا ہو۔ (۴) ایسا جانور نہ ہو جو اپنے دانتوں سے پھاڑ کر کھاتا ہے یا اپنے پنجوں سے نوچ کر کھاتا ہے جیسے شکرہ و باز اور جیسے شیر بھیڑیا وہ ذبح کرنے تک ہاتھ نہ آیا ہو بلکہ شکاری جانور کے مجروح کرنے سے مرچکا ہو تب ہاتھ آیا ہولہذا اگر وہ ہاتھ آیا تو اب بدون ذبح کے حلال نہیں ہے اور اس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اصل میں اپنے ہاتھ سے ذبح کرنا لازم ہے اور جب اختیاری ذبیح ممکن نہ ہو تو اضطراری ذبیجہ تیر و شکاری جانور کے حلا ہو حلال ہو جاتا ہے تو جب اس نے شکاری جانور چھوڑا اور اس نے پکڑا اور مالک پہنچ گیا حالانکہ ابھی شکار زندہ ہے تو اب اس پر اختیاری ذبح کرنا واجب ہے حتی کہ اگر وہ مرگیا بدون ذبح کے تو مردار ہو گیا۔
فصل في الجوارح
ترجمہ فصل ہے جوارح کے بیان میں
تشریح اس فصل میں مصنف ان جانورں سے شکار کرنے کو بیان فرمائیں گے جو زخمی کرنیوالے ہیں اور جوارح جارحہ کی جمع ہے جس
کے دو معنی آتے ہیں ا کسب کرنے والا
زخمی کرنے والا
اور یہاں دونوں ہی معنی مراد ہیں ( کما سیاتی) پھر جوارح کو رمی پر مقدم کیا اس لئے کہ جوارح حیوان جو فاضل ہے اور رمی غیر حیوان ہے جو مفضول ہے اور فاضل مفضول پر مقدم ہوتا ہی ہے۔
کلب، فهد ، بازی ، اور تمام جوارح معلمہ سے شکار جائز ہے
قال يجوز الاصطياد بالكلب المعلم والفهد والبازى وسائر الجوارح المعلمة وفي الجامع الصغير وكل شئی علمته من ذي ناب من السباع وذى مخلب من الطيور فلا باس بصيده ولا خير فيما سوى ذلك الا ان تدرك ذكاته
ترجمہ فرمایا قدوری نے اور کلب معلم سے اور چیتے سے اور باز سے اور سکھائے ہوئے جانوروں سے شکار کرنا جائز ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ہے اور ہر وہ چیز جس کو تو نے تعلیم دیدی یعنی درندوں میں سے دانت والا اور پرندوں میں سے چنگل والا تو اس کے شکار میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور اس کے علاوہ میں کوئی خیر نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ تو اس کی زکاۃ کو پالے۔ تشریح جس کو آپ نے تعلیم دیدی (جس کی تفصیل ابھی آرہی ہے ) خواہ وہ شکار کرنے والا درندہ ہو یا پرندہ ہو تو اس کا کیا ہوا شکار حلال ہے اول کو ڈی ناب اور ثانی کو ذی مخلب کہا جاتا ہے۔
And upon its permissibility, consensus has been established, and because it is a type of earning and benefit from what is created for that, and in it is the preservation of the responsible person (mukallaf) and enabling him to fulfill obligations, so it is permissible (mubah), like gathering firewood. Then the entirety of what the book contains is two chapters: one on hunting with predatory animals (jawaarih), and the second on hunting by shooting (ramy). Explanation: These are the fourth and fifth proofs. The first chapter details hunting with predatory animals; the second details hunting with arrows etc. Warning: There are fifteen conditions for its permissibility: five related to the hunter, five related to the dog, and five related to the prey. ... The chapter on predatory animals (jawaarih). Commentary: In this chapter, the author will discuss hunting with animals that wound. 'Jawaarih' is the plural of 'jaarihah', meaning 'one who earns' and 'one who wounds'; both meanings are intended here. Hunting with a trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all trained predatory animals is permissible. He (al-Quduri) said: 'Hunting with a trained dog, cheetah, falcon, and all trained predatory animals is permissible.' In al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Any creature you have trained from among fanged beasts and clawed birds, there is no harm in its hunting; there is no good in other than that unless you reach its slaughter (udrik dakaatahu).'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Sayd (Book of Hunting) from a commentary on al-Hidayah. It presents two proofs for the permissibility of hunting: first, consensus (ijma') among the scholars, and second, that hunting is a type of earning and benefit, analogous to gathering firewood. The benefits include sustaining the mukallaf (legally responsible person) so he can fulfill his religious duties. The author then outlines the structure of the book: two chapters—the first on hunting with predatory animals (jawaarih) and the second on hunting by shooting (ramy). He then lists fifteen conditions for the permissibility of hunting, divided into three groups of five: conditions related to the hunter (e.g., being eligible for dhabh, releasing the animal, not sharing with someone whose hunting is impermissible, saying tasmiyah, and not engaging in other actions between release and catching); conditions related to the dog (e.g., being trained, following the set path, not being joined by an untrained dog, wounding the prey, and not eating from it); and conditions related to the prey (e.g., not being an insect, not being a sea creature other than fish, being able to defend itself with limbs/horns, not being a predator that tears with fangs or claws, and not being reachable alive for slaughter—if reachable alive, it must be slaughtered). The passage then transitions to the chapter on jawaarih, defining jawaarih as animals that both earn and wound, and establishing the permissibility of hunting with trained dogs, cheetahs, falcons, and all such trained animals. It quotes al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, limiting permissible hunting to animals with fangs (from beasts) or claws (from birds) that are trained. If the hunter reaches the prey alive, he must slaughter it; otherwise, if it dies from the animal's wound, it is halal.

Key Terms
جوارح (jawaarih): Plural of jaarihah; animals that wound or earn, i.e., predatory animals and birds of prey used for hunting.
ذو ناب (dhu naab): A beast with fangs or canines, such as a dog or cheetah.
ذو مخلب (dhu mikhlab): A bird with claws or talons, such as a falcon or hawk.
معلّم (mu'allam): Trained; an animal that has been taught to hunt and responds to commands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two proofs does the passage provide for the permissibility of hunting?
A) Quran and Sunnah
B) Ijma and Istihsan
C) Qiyas and Istihsan
D) Ijma and Qiyas

Key Takeaway
Hunting is mubah by ijma and istihsan, but its permissibility is conditional upon fulfilling fifteen specific conditions.

intermediate

The Fifteen Conditions for Halal Hunting
Listing the fifteen conditions for permissible hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and apply the fifteen conditions for halal hunting as stated in the Hanafi school, categorizing them into hunter, animal, and prey conditions.

Core Idea
Hunting requires fifteen conditions: five for the hunter, five for the hunting animal, and five for the prey.

In the previous lesson, we established that hunting is mubah in principle. Now we delve into the detailed conditions that determine whether a specific hunt yields halal meat. The passage lists fifteen conditions, grouped into three sets of five. Understanding these conditions is crucial for any Hanafi hunter or consumer of hunted meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of conditions
The passage divides the fifteen conditions into three groups: (1) conditions related to the hunter, (2) conditions related to the hunting animal (dog or bird), and (3) conditions related to the prey. Recognize this tripartite structure.
The Arabic text says: 'ان میں سے پانچ وہ ہیں جن کا تعلق بیکاری سے ہے ... اور پانچ شرطیں وہ ہیں جن کا تعلق کتے سے ہے ...'
2
List the five conditions of the hunter
The hunter must: (1) be eligible for dhabh (i.e., Muslim or Kitabi), (2) personally release the animal, (3) not share the act with someone whose hunting is impermissible, (4) recite tasmiyah, and (5) not engage in other actions between releasing and catching.
If any of these are missing, the hunted animal is not halal.
3
List the five conditions of the hunting animal
The animal must: (1) be trained (mu'allam), (2) follow the set path when released, (3) not be joined by an untrained animal, (4) wound the prey (not kill by weight), and (5) not eat from the prey.
Condition 4: The animal must wound the prey; if it kills by mere pressure, the prey is carrion.
4
List the five conditions of the prey
The prey must: (1) not be an insect (hasharat al-ard), (2) not be a sea creature other than fish, (3) be capable of self-defense (i.e., not helpless like a tied animal), (4) not be a predator that tears with fangs or claws (e.g., lion, wolf, hawk), and (5) not be reachable alive for slaughter (if reachable alive, it must be slaughtered, otherwise carrion).
Condition 5 is critical: if the hunter reaches the prey alive, dhabh becomes wajib.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Take a scenario and check each condition. For example, a trained falcon catches a rabbit, eats from it, and the hunter reaches it dead. The violation of condition (5) of the animal (eating) makes the rabbit haram.
Practice ensures you don't overlook any condition.

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Sayd (Book of Hunting) from a commentary on al-Hidayah. It presents two proofs for the permissibility of hunting: first, consensus (ijma') among the scholars, and second, that hunting is a type of earning and benefit, analogous to gathering firewood. Ruling on Hunting with Untrained Animals and Proof from Quran and Hadith
States ruling and provides textual evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hunting with untrained predatory animals and explain the Quranic and hadith evidence that supports the generality of 'jawarih'.

Core Idea
Untrained predators' catch is haram; trained ones are halal because 'jawarih' includes all earners, not just dogs.

Hunting with predatory animals is a practice with specific legal conditions. This passage establishes the foundational ruling that the catch of an untrained animal is impermissible, and then provides the Quranic verse (5:4) and a supporting hadith as evidence. The key interpretive move is that the term 'jawarih' (predatory animals) is general, encompassing any trained animal that hunts by earning, and the term 'mukallibin' means 'senders' rather than 'dog owners'. This sets the stage for the Hanafi position that all trained predators, including lions and falcons, are permissible, not just dogs.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on untrained predators
Identify the primary ruling: if the animal is not trained (ghayr mu'allam), its catch is haram. Note the exception: if the prey is found alive and slaughtered, it becomes halal.
2
Identify the primary proof
Locate the Quranic verse (5:4) cited as the basis. Recognize that this is the foundational dalil for the permissibility of trained predators.
The verse: 'And what you have taught of the predatory animals, training them...'
3
Analyze the key terms: 'jawarih' and 'mukallibin'
Understand that 'jawarih' (pl. of jarihah) are 'earners' – animals that hunt using claws and fangs. 'Mukallibin' is interpreted as 'senders' (musallitin), not specifically dog-owners. This linguistic analysis allows the ruling to apply to all trained predators, not just dogs.
The hadith of 'Adi and the incident of 'Utbah (where 'kalb' is used for lion) reinforce the generality of the term.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Recognize that some schools restrict permissibility to dogs only, while the Hanafi school includes all trained predators. The generality of the Quranic phrase is decisive for Hanafis.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of 'mukallibin'.
5
Assess the Hanafi position on the generality
Confirm that the Hanafi position is that any trained predatory animal is permissible for hunting, provided it has been properly taught to respond to commands and catch the prey. The ruling is mufta bihi.
The passage notes that Imam Abu Hanifah also considers wounding (jarh) as part of the meaning, to be elaborated later.

كتاب الصيد
اور اگر یہ تعلیم یافتہ نہ ہوں تو پھر ان کے شکار میں بھلائی نہیں ہے یعنی حلال نہیں ہے بلکہ حرام ہے ہاں اگر غیر معلم نے شکار پکڑا اور وہ شکار آپ کو زندہ ہل گیا اور آپ نے اس کو ذبح کر دیا تو حلال ہے۔
مذکورہ جانوروں کے شکار کی حلت پر دلیل
والاصل فيه قوله تعالى وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين والجوارح الكواسب في تاويل والمكلبين المسلطين فيتناول الكل بعمومه دل عليه ماروينا من حديث عدى رضى الله عنه واسم الكلب في اللغة يقع على كل سبع حتى الاسد
ترجمہ اور اصل اس میں (یعنی اس میں کہ جارح کا ذی ناب اور ذی مخلب ہونا شرط ہے) اللہ تعالی کا فرمان ہے وما علمتم الخ ۔ اور جوارح بمعنی کو اسب ہے کمائی کرنے والے ایک تاویل کے مطابق اور مسکلمبین مسلطین کے معنی میں ہے ( اور جب معنی وہ ہیں جو ہم نے ذکر کئے ) تو فرمان باری شامل ہو گا تمام جوارح کو اپنے عموم کی وجہ سے اور اسی عموم پر دال ہے وہ حدیث جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں عدی کی حدیث اس لئے اس میں ہے ( اذا ارسلت کلبک اور لفظ کلب لغت میں ہر درندہ پر بولا جاتا ہے یہاں تک کہ شیر کے اوپر ۔ تشریح متن میں جو مسئلہ مذکور ہے اس میں شکاری جانور کا ذی ناب اور ذی مخلب ہونا شرط ہے اور یہ شرط اس آیت سے ثابت ہے جس میں جوارح کا ذکر ہے اور مسکلمین کا جوارح تمام ان جانوروں کو شامل ہے جو اپنے دانت اور چنگل سے شکار کرنے والے ہیں چونکہ جوارح کو اسب کے معنی میں ہے اور شکار کرنا کمائی ہے تو یہ سب جانور کی کمائی کرنے والے ہیں اور یہاں مکلمبین کے معنی کتے کے نہیں بلکہ اس کے معنی ہیں مسلطین یعنی آپ ان جوارح کو شکار پر چھوڑو اور ان کو شکار پر مسلط کرد تاویل کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ بعض حضرات نے جو ارخ بمعنی زخمی کرنے والے کے بھی لئے ہیں ( کماسیا تی )۔
بہر حال جب آیت کے معنی یہ ہوئے جو مذکور ہیں تو اسکے عموم میں تمام جوارح داخل ہیں اور یہ حکم صرف کتوں کے لئے مخصوص نہیں رہا۔ اور حضرت عدی کی حدیث بھی اسی عموم پر دال ہے جس میں لفظ کلب لغت میں تمام درندوں کو کہا جاتا ہے جس میں شیر بھی داخل ہے۔ ا آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عتبہ بن ابو لہب کے بارے میں فرمایا تھا " اللهم سلط عليه كلبا من كلا بک" تو اللہ نے اس پر شیر کو مسلط فرما دیا تھا اور شیر نے اس کو پھاڑ دیا تھا۔
تنبیہ - ۲ پوری آیت یہ ہے۔ یسئلونک ماذا احل لهم قل احل لكم الطيبات وما علمتم من الجوارح مكلبين تعلمو نهن مما عَلَمَكُمُ الله فكلوا مما امسكن عليكم واذكروا اسم الله عليه
لوگ تجھ سے پوچھتے ہیں کہ ان کے لئے کیا چیز حلال ہے آپ فرمائیے کہ تمہارے پاکیزہ چیز میں حلال ہیں اور جو تم سکھاؤ شکاری جانور شکار پر دوڑانے کو کہ تم ان کو سکھاتے ہو ان باتوں میں سے جو اللہ نے تم کو سکھائی ہیں تو تم کھاؤ اس میں سے جو دہ پکڑے رکھیں تمہارے واسطے اور اس پر اللہ کا نام لو۔
بہر حال لفظ جوارح اپنے مادہ جرح کے اعتبار سے اس کو بھی شامل ہے کہ شکاری جانور شکار کو زخمی بھی کر دے اور یہی امام ابوحنیفہ کا مذہب ہے جس کی تفصیل ابھی آ رہی ہے۔
And if these are not trained, then there is no goodness in their hunt, i.e., it is not permissible, rather it is haram. However, if an untrained animal catches prey and that prey moves alive and you slaughter it, then it is halal.
Evidence for the permissibility of hunting with the mentioned animals:
And the basis for this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And what you have taught of the predatory animals, training them...' (Quran 5:4). Al-Jawarih are the earners, in interpretation, and al-mukallibin means those who send, so it includes all by its generality. This is supported by what we narrated from the hadith of 'Adi (may Allah be pleased with him), and the word 'kalb' in language applies to every beast of prey, even the lion.
Translation: And the basis in this (i.e., that the predator must have fangs and claws) is the command of Allah: 'And what you have taught...' etc. Al-Jawarih means earners, according to an interpretation, and al-mukallibin means senders. When the meaning is as we mentioned, the divine command includes all jawarih because of its generality, and that generality is indicated by the hadith we narrated, the hadith of 'Adi, because in it is (when you send your dog), and the word 'kalb' in language is used for every beast, even the lion.
Commentary: In the text, the mentioned ruling requires the hunting animal to have fangs and claws, and this condition is proven from the verse that mentions jawarih and mukallibin. Jawarih includes all animals that hunt with their teeth and claws. Since jawarih means earners, and hunting is earning, these animals are earners. And here mukallibin does not mean dogs, but rather it means senders, i.e., you release these jawarih upon the prey and set them upon it. The restriction of tawiyl (interpretation) is because some scholars have taken jarh to mean wounder (kamasati?). In any case, when the meaning of the verse is as mentioned, its generality includes all jawarih, and this ruling is not specific only to dogs. And the hadith of 'Adi also indicates this generality, in which the word 'kalb' is applied in language to all beasts, including the lion. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding 'Utbah ibn Abi Lahab: 'O Allah, set upon him a dog from among Your dogs,' so Allah set a lion upon him, and the lion tore him apart.
Note: The full verse is: 'They ask you what has been made lawful for them. Say: Lawful for you are good foods and what you have taught of predatory animals, training them; you teach them from what Allah has taught you. So eat of what they catch for you, and mention the name of Allah upon it.' (Quran 5:4). In any case, the word jawarih, based on its root jarh, also includes the fact that the predatory animal wounds the prey, and this is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifah, the details of which are coming.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by stating that if predatory animals used for hunting are not trained (ghayr mu'allam), their catch is not halal but haram. However, if the animal catches prey and it is found alive and then slaughtered properly, it becomes halal. This ruling is based on the Quranic verse (5:4) which mentions 'jawarih' (predatory animals) and 'mukallibin' (those who send them). The term 'jawarih' includes all animals that hunt by earning, i.e., using their claws and fangs. The verse is general and covers all such animals, not just dogs. The Prophet's hadith about 'Utbah ibn Abi Lahab, where the word 'kalb' is used for a lion, further supports the generality. The commentator interprets 'mukallibin' as 'senders' (musallitin), meaning the hunter releases the animal upon the prey. This interpretation is necessary because some understood 'jarh' as 'wounding', but here it is about training and sending. The Hanafi position is that any predatory animal that can be trained and catches prey is permissible, provided it is trained. The passage ends by noting that the word 'jawarih' also implies wounding, which is Imam Abu Hanifah's view, to be elaborated later.

Key Terms
جوارح (jawarih): Predatory animals that hunt by earning (using claws/fangs); plural of jarihah.
مكلبين (mukallibin): Those who send the jawarih upon the prey; interpreted as musallitin (senders), not specifically dog-owners.
تعلیم (ta'lim): Training the predatory animal to respond to commands, catch, and retain prey for its owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the catch of an untrained predatory animal according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is halal without any condition
B) It is haram unless the prey is found alive and slaughtered
C) It is makruh tanzihi
D) It is halal if the animal is a dog

Key Takeaway
The catch of an untrained predatory animal is haram, but if trained, it is halal based on the general Quranic ruling covering all 'jawarih'.

Exceptions to Permissible Hunting Animals and the Condition of Training
Specifies animals excluded and condition of training

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exceptions to permissible hunting animals in the Hanafi school and explain how the condition of training can override certain exclusions.

Core Idea
Pig is always haram; lion, bear, and kite become halal if they accept training.

The general rule in the Hanafi school is that hunting with trained predatory animals (jawarih) is permissible. However, there are specific exceptions. Imam Abu Yusuf excluded certain animals due to their nature, but later Hanafi authorities qualified this exclusion. Understanding these nuances is essential for determining the halal status of game caught by these animals. This lesson clarifies which animals are excluded and under what conditions they become permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exceptions
Start with the principle that hunting with trained jawarih is allowed. Then list the animals Abu Yusuf excluded: lion, bear, and kite (the latter added by some). Also note the pig is excluded absolutely.
The pig is excluded because it is najis al-ayn, not due to training issues.
2
Understand the basis for each exception
Analyze why Abu Yusuf excluded lion, bear, and kite: lion due to high spirit (does not work for others), bear and kite due to baseness. The pig is excluded due to intrinsic impurity.
The reasoning for lion, bear, and kite is based on their nature, not a textual prohibition.
3
Apply the condition of training
Training (ta'lim) is an essential condition derived from Quran and hadith. If the animal accepts training and is sent (irsal) by the hunter, it becomes a valid instrument of slaughter. This overrides the natural exclusion for lion, bear, and kite.
The later Hanafi position (mufta bihi) holds that if these animals accept training, their catch is halal.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute and the mufta bihi
Distinguish Abu Yusuf's default exclusion from the later view that allows training to override it. Note that the pig remains haram even if trained.
The relied-upon position is found in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Shami: if lion, bear, or kite accept training, their catch is halal.

Source Text

وعن ابى يوسف انه استثنى من ذلك الاسد والدب لانهما لا يعملان لغيرهما الأسد لعلو همته والدب لخساسته والحق بهما بعضهم الحدأة لخساسته والخنزير مستثنى لانه نجس العين فلا يجوز الانتفاع به ثم الة لابد من التعليم لان ما تلونا من النص ينطق باشتراط التعليم والحديث به وبالارسال ولانه انما يصير بالتعليم ليكون عاملا له فيترسل بارساله ويمسكه عليه
ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ انہوں نے جوارح سے شیر اور ریچھ کا استثناء کیا ہے اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں اپنے غیر کے لئے کام نہیں کرتے شیر اپنی ہمت کی بلندی کی وجہ سے اور کچھ اپنے کمینہ پن کی وجہ سے اور لاحق کر دیا ان دونوں کے ساتھ ان میں سے بعض نے چیل کو اس کمینہ پن کی وجہ سے اور خنزیر ( آیت کے عموم سے مستثنیٰ ہے اس لئے کہ وہ نجس العین ہے تو اس سے انتفاع جائز نہیں ہے پھر تعلیم کا ہونا ضروری ہے اس لئے کہ جو ص ہم نے تلاوت کیا ہے وہ تعلیم کے شرط ہونے پر دال ہے اور حدیث تعلیم کے اور ارسال کے شرط ہونے پر دال ہے اور اس لئے کہ شکاری جانور تعلیم کی وجہ سے آلہ ذکات بنے گا تا کہ وہ مرسل کے لئے عامل ہو جائے پس وہ رواں ہو جائے شکاری کے چھوڑنے سے اور شکار کو اپنے مالک کے لئے روک لے۔
تشریح تمام جوارح سے شکار کرنا جائز ہے مگر ان میں سے شیر اور کچھ اور چیل مستثنیٰ ہے کیونکہ یہ دوسرے کے لئے کام نہیں کرتے شیر تو اپنی بہادری کی وجہ سے اور کچھ اور چیل اپی کمینگی کی وجہ سے اور خنزیر بھی متقی ہے کیونکہ وہ نجس العین ہے جس سے نفع اٹھا نا حلال نہیں ہے پھر تعلیم کا ہونا اور شکاری کی طرف سے ارسال کا ہونا ضروری ہے آیت مذکورہ تعلیم پر او حدیث علمی تعلیم ارسال دونوں پر دال ہے۔ اور شکاری جانور ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ شکاری خود اپنی چھری وغیرہ سے ذبح کر رہا ہے بالفاظ دیگر جب جانور نے آدمی کی خوسیکھ لی وہ ذبح میں آدمی کے قائم مقام ہو گیا مگر اس نیابت کے لئے تعلیم شرط ہے تعلیم کے بعد ہی وہ مرسل کے لئے کام کرے گا اس کے چھوڑنے شکار پر پڑے گا اور پھر شکار کو اس لئے روک رکھیںگا۔
تنبیه در مختار اور شامی میں مسئلہ بیان کرنے کا طریقہ اختیار کیا گیا ہے۔ کہ ہر ذی ناب اور ذی مخلب کا شکار جائز ہے کچھ شرطوں کے ساتھ شرط اول یہ کہ وہ شکاری جانور نجس العین نہ ہو اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ اس میں تعلیم کو قبول کرنے کی صلاحیت ہو تو اس بیان سے خنزیر سے انتفاع حرام ہے اس لئے کہ وہ نجس العین ہے تو اس کا شکار بہر صورت حرام ہوگا اگر چہ وہ تعلیم قبول کرے اور اگر چہ کتے کو بھی بعض فقہاء نے نجس العین قرار دیا ہے، مگر اس سے شکار بالا تفاق جائز ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ کتے کے سلسلہ میں نص وارد ہے۔ اور خنزیر کے سلسلہ میں کوئی نص وارد نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر شیر اور کچھ اور بھٹر یا غیر تعلیم کوقبول کر لیں اور انکا معلم ہونا معلوم ہو جائے تو پھر ان کا شکار حلال ہوگا کذا صرح فی الشامی ص ۲۹۸ ج ۵
And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he excluded from that the lion and the bear, because they do not work for others; the lion due to its high spirit, and the bear due to its baseness. And some joined to them the kite due to its baseness. And the pig is excluded because it is impure in itself (najis al-ayn), so it is not permissible to benefit from it. Then, the tool (the animal) must be trained, because the text we recited indicates the condition of training, and the hadith indicates both training and sending. And because only through training does it become an instrument of slaughter, so that it acts for the sender; thus it goes at his sending and holds the prey for him.
Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he excluded from the jawarih the lion and the bear, because these two do not work for others; the lion due to the height of its ambition, and the bear due to its baseness. And some joined to them the kite due to its baseness. And the pig is excluded from the generality of the verse because it is impure in itself, so benefiting from it is not permissible. Then, training is necessary because the verse we recited indicates the condition of training, and the hadith indicates both training and sending. And because only through training does the predatory animal become an instrument of slaughter, so that it becomes an agent for the sender; then it goes at his sending and holds the prey for his owner.
Commentary: Hunting with all jawarih is permissible, but among them the lion, bear, and kite are exceptions because they do not work for others; the lion due to its bravery, and the bear and kite due to their baseness. And the pig is also excluded because it is impure in itself, from which benefiting is not halal. Then, training and sending by the hunter are necessary. The mentioned verse indicates training, and the hadith indicates both training and sending. The predatory animal becomes as if the hunter is slaughtering with his own knife; in other words, when the animal learns from man, it becomes a substitute for him in slaughter. But for this deputyship, training is a condition. Only after training will it work for the sender; it will pounce when released and then hold the prey for him.
Note: In al-Mukhtar and al-Shami, the method of stating the ruling is that hunting with every animal with fangs and claws is permissible with certain conditions: first, that the predatory animal is not impure in itself; second, that it has the capacity to accept training. According to this, benefiting from pig is haram because it is impure in itself, so its hunting is absolutely haram even if it accepts training. And even though some jurists have declared the dog impure in itself, hunting with it is unanimously permissible, because there is a specific text (nass) regarding dogs. There is no such text regarding pigs. However, if lions, bears, or others accept training and become known as trained, then their hunting will be halal. Thus it is explicitly stated in al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 298.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage deals with exceptions to the general permissibility of hunting with jawarih and the essential condition of training. Imam Abu Yusuf excludes the lion and the bear from the general ruling because they do not work for others; the lion due to its proud nature and the bear due to its baseness. Some scholars also exclude the kite (hawk-like bird) for baseness. The pig is excluded because it is najis al-ayn (impure in essence), so no benefit from it is permissible, even if trained. Then the passage emphasizes that training (ta'lim) is absolutely necessary. The Quranic verse explicitly requires training, and the hadith adds the condition of sending (irsal). Through training, the animal becomes a substitute for the hunter's hand in slaughtering. The commentator clarifies that if animals like lions or bears actually accept training and become known as trained, their catch becomes halal, contrary to Abu Yusuf's default exclusion. This is based on later Hanafi texts like al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Shami. The pig remains haram even if trained due to its intrinsic impurity, while the dog is an exception because of a specific Prophetic text allowing its use despite its impurity. The passage thus balances general principles with specific evidence.

Key Terms
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): Impure in essence; the animal itself is impure, so no benefit is permissible.
ارسال (irsal): Sending the trained animal upon the prey; a condition for the catch to be halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as detailed in the passage, what is the ruling on hunting with a pig that has been trained?
A) Halal because it is trained
B) Haram because it is impure in essence
C) Makruh tahrimi
D) Halal only if sent by the hunter

Key Takeaway
Hunting with pig is always haram; animals like lion, bear, and kite can become halal if they accept training.

Prohibited Hunting Animals and Necessity of Training
Explanation of exceptions from jawarih and requirement of ta'leem

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding permissible hunting animals, and apply the conditions of ta'leem and najasah to determine the ruling for a given animal.

Core Idea
A hunting animal must be trainable and not najis al-ayn; lion and bear become permissible if trained.

This lesson examines which animals can be used as hunting instruments (jawarih) according to the Hanafi school. The primary sources—Quran and Hadith—permit hunting with trained animals, but the pig is absolutely excluded due to its inherent impurity. Within the school, there is a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the lion, bear, and hawk. Understanding this ikhtilaf and the role of training (ta'leem) is essential for correctly applying the rules of hunting.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi ruling on jawarih
Identify that the word jawarih includes any animal that wounds prey, and that hunting with any trained jarih is generally permissible except for the pig.
This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's exception and its rationale
Note that Abu Yusuf excludes the lion, bear, and hawk because they do not work for others—lion due to pride, bear and hawk due to lowliness.
Some later scholars also add the hawk to the exception.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response and the role of training
Examine the counter-argument: if these animals accept training and their training is known, they become like other trained jawarih and their hunting is Halal.
The relied-upon position in Shami adopts this view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Conclude that the operative ruling for fatwa is that hunting with lion, bear, or cheetah is permissible if they have been properly trained.
The pig remains absolutely haram because it is najis al-ayn.
5
Apply the conditions to new cases
Test the ruling on other animals: e.g., a trained hawk or cheetah. Ensure the conditions of not being najis al-ayn and acceptance of training are met.
The dog, though considered najis by some, is allowed due to explicit textual permission.

However, the word 'jawarih' from its root 'jarh' includes that the hunting animal wounds the prey, and this is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa, the details of which are coming. From which animals is hunting not permissible? And from Abu Yusuf that he excepted from that the lion and the bear because they do not work for others - the lion due to high spirit and the bear due to lowliness. And some added to them the hawk due to lowliness. And the pig is excepted because it is najis al-ayn, so benefiting from it is not permissible. Then the instrument must have training because the verse we recited indicates the condition of training, and the hadith indicates the condition of training and sending, and because by training it becomes an instrument of slaughter for him, so it acts for him, it is sent by his sending and holds the prey for him. Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he excepted from jawarih the lion and the bear because they do not work for others; the lion due to high spirit and the bear due to lowliness. And some among them added the hawk due to its lowliness. And the pig is excepted from the general meaning of the verse because it is najis al-ayn, so benefiting from it is not permissible. Then training is necessary because the verse we recited indicates the condition of training, and the hadith indicates the condition of training and sending, and because the hunting animal by training becomes an instrument of slaughter, so that it acts for the sender, then it runs when the hunter releases it and holds the prey for its owner. Explanation: Hunting with all jawarih is permissible except among them the lion, bear, and hawk because they do not work for others; the lion due to its bravery, bear and hawk due to their lowliness. And the pig is also excepted because it is najis al-ayn, from which benefiting is not halal. Then training and sending by the hunter are necessary. The mentioned verse indicates training, and the hadith indicates both training and sending. And the hunting animal becomes as if the hunter himself is slaughtering with his knife etc. In other words, when the animal has learned from man, it is deputized for man in slaughter, but for this deputization training is a condition. After training, it will work for the sender, pounce on the prey when released, and then hold the prey for him. Note: In Durr al-Mukhtar and Shami, the method of stating the issue is adopted: that hunting with every animal with fangs or claws is permissible with some conditions. First condition: that the hunting animal is not najis al-ayn. Second condition: that it has the ability to accept training. So from this statement, benefiting from the pig is haram because it is najis al-ayn, so its hunting is haram in all cases even if it accepts training. And although some jurists consider the dog to be najis al-ayn, hunting with it is unanimously permissible because the dog is mentioned in the text, while there is no text about the pig. However, if a lion, bear, or cheetah accept training and their being trained is known, then their hunting becomes halal. As explicitly stated in Shami, vol. 5, p. 298.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, begins the Book of Hunting by discussing which animals can be used as hunting instruments (jawarih). The author first notes that the word jawarih includes any animal that wounds its prey, which is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. He then reports a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf who excepts the lion and the bear from the permissible hunting animals because they do not work for others; the lion is too proud and the bear too lowly. Some scholars also add the hawk for its lowliness. The pig is absolutely excluded because it is najis al-ayn (impure in essence), so no benefit from it is permitted. After these exceptions, the passage emphasizes the necessity of training (ta'leem) for any hunting animal. This is proven by the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah:4) about taught hunting animals and by the hadith that also requires sending (irsal). The reasoning is that training makes the animal act as an instrument of slaughter on behalf of the hunter, akin to a knife. The note (tanbeeh) from Durr al-Mukhtar and Shami further clarifies that the permissibility of hunting with any animal with fangs or claws depends on two conditions: the animal is not najis al-ayn and can accept training. Thus the pig is always haram, while the dog, despite some considering it najis, is allowed due to textual evidence. The note adds that if a lion, bear, or cheetah are trained, their hunting becomes halal. This lesson shows the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from primary texts and the hierarchy of opinions within the school.

Key Terms
جوارح (jawarih): Hunting animals that wound prey, including dogs, birds of prey, etc.
تعلیم (ta'leem): Training of a hunting animal so that it acts on behalf of the hunter.
نجس العین (najis al-ayn): Impure in essence; refers to the pig which cannot be purified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hunting with an animal depends on it being not najis al-ayn and capable of training; the lion and bear become permissible if properly trained.

Training of Dog vs. Falcon: Conditions and Rationale
Explanation of difference in training signs between dog and falcon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for training a dog and a falcon for hunting and explain the rationale for the different signs.

Core Idea
A dog is trained by leaving its prey three times; a falcon by returning when called — nature dictates the method.

In Hanafi fiqh, hunting with trained animals is permitted only if the animal is properly trained. The signs of training differ based on the animal's nature and physical constitution. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the text, the transmitted proof from Ibn Abbas, and the rational justification that leads to the condition of three times for the dog and returning for the falcon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
The act being ruled upon is the permissibility of hunting with a trained animal. The training condition is a prerequisite for the prey to be halal.
This falls under Kitab al-Sayd (Book of Hunting).
2
State the dog training condition
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and a narration from Abu Hanifa, a dog is considered trained when it leaves eating the prey three times.
The text emphasizes 'ثلث مرات' (three times).
3
State the falcon training condition
A falcon is considered trained when it returns when called. Its delicate body cannot bear beating, so domestication is the sign.
The falcon's sign is returning, not refraining from eating.
4
Examine the proof
The text attributes this distinction to a narration from Ibn Abbas. Allama Zayla'i notes he did not find it, but the Hanafi school still uses it as a basis, supported by rational analysis.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi, considered zanni al-thubut but accepted.
5
Analyze the rationale
The difference is based on animal nature: dogs are robust and accustomed to humans, so training requires suppressing their instinct to eat prey; falcons are wild and delicate, so responding to a call indicates domestication.
Maqasid: training signs align with the animal's innate disposition.

Book of Eid? (heading) Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 14. Difference in training of dog and falcon. And he said: The training of the dog is that it leaves eating three times, and the training of the falcon is that it returns and responds when you call it. And this is narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him. Translation: The training of a dog is that it leaves eating three times, and the training of a falcon is that it returns and answers when you call it (i.e., comes back). And this detail is narrated from Ibn Abbas. Explanation: There is a difference between the training of a dog and a falcon. A dog is considered trained when the effect of training and discipline appears on it such that it catches the prey and does not eat it but holds it for the owner, and this action has occurred from it three times. The training of a falcon is that it comes when you call it. The author says that this detail is narrated from Ibn Abbas. Allama Zayla'i says about this narration: 'I have not found it.' The face of difference: And because the body of the falcon cannot bear beating, while the body of the dog can bear it, so the dog is beaten to make it leave eating. And because the sign of training is leaving what is its usual habit. The falcon is wild and averse to humans, so its responding is the sign of its training. As for the dog, it is accustomed to humans and used to plundering, so the sign of its training is leaving its usual habit, which is eating and snatching. Translation: And because the body of the falcon cannot bear beating, and the body of the dog can bear beating, so the dog is beaten so that it leaves eating. And because the sign of training is leaving what is its usual desired thing. The falcon is wild and averse to humans, so its returning is the sign of its training. In any case, the dog is tamed and used to plundering, so the sign of its training is leaving its desired thing which is eating and snatching. Explanation: Then the difference between dog and falcon is made because it is easy to train a dog well because it can tolerate beating, while the body of the falcon cannot tolerate beating. The second point is that the sign of training is that the animal refrains from its desired habit and natural habit. Since the dog is already accustomed to humans, coming when called is not a sign of its training. However, the dog's habit is to eat whatever it gets and to plunder, so when it catches the prey and does not eat it, that is a sign of its being trained and disciplined. The falcon, being a wild bird, when it becomes so familiar with you that it comes when called, that alone is considered the sign of its training. When is a dog considered trained? Statements of jurists: Then the condition of leaving eating three times. This is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and a narration from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on them, because in them there is something more.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya continues the discussion on hunting, specifically the training (ta'leem) of hunting animals. The text begins with a quote from the matn (probably from al-Quduri): 'The training of a dog is that it leaves eating three times, and the training of a falcon is that it returns when called.' This is attributed to a narration from Ibn Abbas, though Allama Zayla'i notes he did not find it. The commentary then explains the wisdom behind the difference. The dog's body can withstand beating, so it is disciplined by force to stop eating the prey. The falcon's body is delicate, so its training relies on domestication: returning when called. The dog, being naturally accustomed to humans, does not signal training by merely coming when called; rather, it must overcome its natural instinct to consume the prey. Hence, the dog must leave eating the prey three times to be considered trained. The falcon, being wild, signals training by simply responding to the call. The passage ends by stating that the condition of leaving eating three times is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) and a narration from Abu Hanifa. This reflects the Hanafi methodology of integrating textual transmission (Ibn Abbas) with rational analysis of animal behavior.

Key Terms
تعلیم (ta'leem): The specific signs that indicate a hunting animal is trained.
باز (baz): Falcon or hawk used for hunting.
ثلث مرات (thulth marrat): Three times; the number of times a dog must leave eating to be considered trained.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the falcon's training judged by its returning when called, while the dog's training is judged by leaving eating?
A) Because the falcon is wild and the dog is tame
B) Because the falcon cannot be beaten
C) Both A and B
D) Because the falcon does not eat meat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes training signs based on animal nature: a dog must leave eating prey three times; a falcon must return when called — a condition supported by transmitted narration and rational analysis.

Distinction Between Training a Dog and a Falcon
Definition of training signs for dog and falcon with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the signs of ta'leem (training) for a dog and a falcon according to the Hanafi school, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the distinction.

Core Idea
A dog is trained when it leaves prey three times; a falcon is trained when it returns when called — because their natures differ.

The permissibility of eating game caught by a trained hunting animal depends on the animal being properly trained. But what counts as training? The Hanafi school, based on the statement of Ibn Abbas, distinguishes between the training signs for dogs and falcons. In this lesson, we examine that distinction and the underlying reasoning, which is essential for determining whether the meat is halal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two animals and their training signs
Read the passage to extract the specific sign for each animal: three refusals for the dog, response to call for the falcon.
The dog's sign is 'ترك الاكل ثلاث مرات' (leaving eating three times). The falcon's sign is 'يرجع ويجيب' (returns and responds).
2
Examine the legal source (qawl sahabi)
The author attributes this distinction to Ibn Abbas. Evaluate the strength: it is a zanni source, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh as a Companion's statement.
Allamah Zayla'i noted 'لم أجد' (I did not find it), but the ruling is still operative.
3
Understand the reasoning (wajh al-farq)
The passage gives two reasons: physical capacity (the falcon cannot be beaten) and habitual nature (the dog is tame and prone to snatching, the falcon is wild).
This ta'lil shows that training signs are not arbitrary but based on the animal's disposition.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific case, determine whether the animal is considered trained. For a dog, you would count its refusals; for a falcon, check if it returns when called.
5
Note the ikhtilaf (cross-madhhab)
Some other schools may not require three refusals for the dog; they might consider one or two sufficient. The Hanafi position is based on the prominent narration from Ibn Abbas.
Thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in cases where the dog has refused only twice.

Source Text

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور کتے کی تعلیم یہ ہے کہ وہ تین مرتبہ کھانا چھوڑ دے اور باز کی تعلیم یہ ہے کہ وہ لوٹ جائے اور جب اس کو بلائے تو وہ لبیک کہے ( یعنی واپس آ جائے ) اور یہ تفصیل منقول ہے ابن عباس ہے۔

وجه فرق
ولان بدن البازي لا يحتمل الضرب وبدن الكلب يحتمله فيضرب ليتركه ولان اية التعليم ترك ما هو مالوفه عادة والبازى متوحش متنفر فكانت الاجابة آية تعليمه اما الكلب فهو الوف يعتاد الانتهاب فكان اية تعلیمه ترک مالوفه وهو الاكل والاستلاب
And he said: The training of a dog is that it leaves eating three times, and the training of a falcon is that it returns and responds when called. And this is narrated from Ibn Abbas (رضي الله عنه). Translation: Al-Quduri said: The training of a dog is that it leaves food three times, and the training of a falcon is that it returns and responds when called. And this detail is narrated from Ibn Abbas. Explanation: There is a difference between the training of a dog and a falcon. A dog is considered trained when the effect of training and discipline appears: it hunts, does not eat the prey, but restrains it for its owner, and this action occurs three times. The training of a falcon is that it comes when called. The author says this detail is narrated from Ibn Abbas; Allamah Zayla'i says about this athar: 'I did not find it.' The reason for the difference: Because the body of a falcon cannot bear beating, while the body of a dog can bear it, so it is beaten to make it leave. And because the sign of training is leaving what is habitually familiar. The falcon is wild and averse, so responding is the sign of its training. As for the dog, it is tame and accustomed to snatching, so the sign of its training is leaving what is familiar, which is eating and snatching.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling from the text of Al-Quduri, commented upon by the author. It establishes the distinct signs of training (ta'leem) for hunting dogs versus falcons. The dog is considered trained only after it has refrained from eating the prey three consecutive times, indicating it has overcome its natural instinct to consume. The falcon is considered trained when it returns upon being called, reflecting its tamed nature. The author cites Ibn Abbas for this distinction, though Allamah Zayla'i noted he could not find the athar. The reasoning (wajh al-farq) is practical: dogs can be disciplined through beating to abandon eating, but falcons cannot. Moreover, the dog's natural tendency is to snatch and eat, so leaving that demonstrates training; the falcon's wildness means that coming when called is the true sign of domestication. This distinction is crucial for the permissibility of consuming the hunted game.

Key Terms
تعليم (ta'leem): The process of training a hunting animal so that it behaves in a manner indicating it is trained, i.e., the dog leaves prey and the falcon returns when called.
بازي (bāzī): A falcon or trained bird of prey used for hunting.
أكلة (uklah): Eating; in context, the dog's act of consuming the hunted prey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It leaves eating the prey three times.
B) It returns when called.
C) It kills the prey quickly.
D) It does not fly away.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes dog training (three refusals) from falcon training (response to call) based on their physical nature and habits, as narrated from Ibn Abbas.

The Three-Refusal Condition for a Trained Hunting Dog
Intra-Hanafi dispute on quantifying a dog's refusal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of times a dog must refrain from eating prey, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Three refusals establish certainty; fewer leaves doubt. The Hanafi school relies on three.

The training of a hunting dog is judged by its obedience. A key question is how many times it must leave the prey uneaten to prove it is trained. This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute: did the Sahibayn fix three refusals, or is the hunter's opinion enough? Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists balance textual analogy with practical discretion.

Guided Path
1
State the main Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and one narration from Abu Hanifa: the dog must leave the prey three times.
This is the zahir al-riwayah and mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opposing view within the school
Note the second narration from Abu Hanifa (in al-Asl): no fixed number; it depends on the hunter's predominant opinion (zann).
This view leaves the condition open-ended.
3
Examine the proof for the three-refusal condition
The Sahibayn argue that fewer than three leaves probability (ihtimal) that the dog refused due to fullness, not training. Three indicates a habit. They analogize to other three-day criteria in shariah.
Examples: khiyar al-shart, Musa and Khidr, three-day respite for a murtad, minimum menstruation.
4
Examine the opposing proof
The second narration argues that fixed limits are not set by opinion without text; the hunter's confidence (ghalabat al-zann) suffices.
This relies on the principle that quantities are not established by ra'y.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: if a dog refuses only twice, the Sahibayn rule the prey carrion; the other view allows it if the hunter is sure. The mufta bihi is the three-refusal condition for caution and consistency.
The commentator prefers the Sahibayn's view as more precautionary and backed by qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم شرط ترك الاكل ثلثا وهذا عندهما وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة رحمهم الله لان فيهما دونه الاحتمال فلعله ترك مرة او مرتين شبعا فاذا تركه ثلثا دل على انه صار عادة له ولهذا لان الثلث مدة ضربت للاختيار وابلاء الاعذار كما في مدة الخيار وفي بعض قصص الاخيار
ترجمہ پھر قدوری نے شرط لگائی تین مرتبہ چھوڑنے کی اور یہ صاحبین کے نزدیک ہے اور یہی ایک روایت ہے ابو حنیفہ سے اس لئے کہ اس سے کم میں مزید احتمال ہے پس شاید اس نے کھانا چھوڑا ہو ایک یا دو مرتبہ چھکنے کی وجہ سے پس جب اس نے تین مرتبہ کھانا چھوڑ دیا تو یہ اس بات پر دال ہے کہ اس کی عادت بن گئی ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ تین ایسی مدت ہے جس کو آزمائش کے لئے اور اعذار کی جانچ کے لئے مقرر کی گئی ہے جیسے خیار کی مدت میں اور بعض پسندیدہ حضرات کے واقعات میں۔ تشریح کتے کی تعلیم کی شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ تین مرتبہ شکار کو نہ کھائے اور یہ صاحبین کا مذہب ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے اس میں دو قول ہیں ایک تو یہی ہے جو صاحبین کا ہے اور دوسرادہ ہے جو آئندہ آ رہا ہے کہ اس کی کوئی مقدار مقرر نہیں بلکہ یہ رائے مبتلی یہ پر موقوف ہے۔ بہر حال مذہب اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر اس نے ایک یا دو مرتبہ کھانا چھوڑا ہو تو اس میں ابھی بہت سے احتمالات ہیں کہ شاید شکم سیر ہونے کی وجہ سے نہ کھایا ہوا لبتہ جب اس نے تین مرتبہ تک نہیں کھایا تو یہ عادت ہو جانے کی دلیل ہے۔ اور تین کو عادت کے چانچنے میں اور دیگر اعزار میں کافی دخل ہے، حضرت موسیٰ اور حضر کے واقعہ میں بھی تین کا دخل ہے حضرت موسیٰ نے تیسری مرتبہ کے بارے میں کہ دیا تھا کہ ان سألتك عن شئ بعدها.

ولان الكثير هو الذى يقع امارة على العلم دون القليل والجمع هو الكثير وادناه الثلث فقد ربها وعندابي حنيفة على ماذكر في الأصل يثبت التعليم مالم يغلب على ظن الصائد انه معلم ولا يقدر بالثلث لان المقادير لا تعرف اجتهاد ابل نصاوسما عاولا سمع فيفوض الى رأى المبتلى به كما هو اصله في جنسها
Then he stipulated leaving eating three times, and this is according to the two (Sahibayn) and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on them). Because with less than that there is probability; perhaps he left once or twice due to fullness. So when he leaves it three times, it indicates it has become a habit for him. And because three is a period set for testing and excusing, as in the option period and in some stories of the righteous. Translation: Then Al-Quduri stipulated leaving eating three times, and this is according to the Sahibayn and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. Because with less there is more probability; perhaps he left once or twice due to being full. So when he leaves it three times, it indicates it has become his habit. And because three is a period set for testing and excusing, as in the option period (khiyar) and in some stories of the righteous. Explanation: The condition for training a dog is that it does not eat the prey three times. This is the madhhab of the Sahibayn, and Imam Abu Hanifa has two sayings: one is this same, and the other is that no specific number is fixed; rather it depends on the opinion of the one facing the issue. In any case, the proof of the first madhhab is that if it leaves once or twice, there are many possibilities; perhaps it didn't eat due to being full. But when it leaves three times, it is evidence that it has become a habit. And three has great involvement in testing habits and other matters, as in the story of Musa and Khidr: Musa said after the third time: 'If I ask you about anything after this.' Warning: And there are many similar examples: 'Enjoy in your house for three days,' 'Do not speak to people for three days,' 'When one of you asks permission three times and is not permitted, then leave,' 'Whoever fails in a thing three times and does not profit, let him turn to something else,' 'The period of respite for a Murtad is three days,' 'The minimum of menstruation.' (Because) the many (kathir) is that which can be a sign for knowledge, not the few, and the plural is many, and its minimum is three. So it is tied to three. And according to Abu Hanifa, as mentioned in al-Asl, training is established as long as the hunter is fairly certain that it is trained, and it is not limited to three, because measures are not known by opinion without text or hearing. So it is referred to the opinion of the one facing the matter, as is his principle in this kind of matter.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the number of times a trained dog must refrain from eating the prey to be considered reliably trained. The matn stipulates three times, which is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) and also a narration from Abu Hanifa. Their reasoning is that fewer than three leaves room for doubt: the dog may have refrained once or twice due to being full rather than obedience. Three refusals establish a pattern (adah) and remove uncertainty. The author analogizes to other three-based criteria in shariah, such as the option period, Musa's test with Khidr, the three-day respite for a murtad, and the minimum menstruation period. However, the author notes another narration from Abu Hanifa (mentioned in al-Asl) that training is not quantified by three but is left to the hunter's predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann). This is because numerical limits are not established by independent reasoning (ra'y) without textual basis. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn requiring three times, as it is the more cautious and established in the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
كثير (kathīr): Plurality; the minimum of which is three. Used to argue that three is the threshold for a reliable sign.
ظن (zann): Predominant opinion; in the context of Abu Hanifa's view, the hunter's certainty that the dog is trained.
مبتلى به (mubtalā bihī): The person facing the issue (the hunter); his opinion is considered in the second narration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The three-refusal condition is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school for a trained dog, based on the Sahibayn's reasoning that three removes doubt and aligns with shariah patterns.
